class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       (\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\xaa\xc9\x99r/: \'ear\' in \'near\'">\n            \xc9\xaa\xc9\x99r\n           </span>\n           <span title="/i\xcb\x90/ or /\xc9\xaa/: \'y\' in \'happy\'">\n            i\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">\n        French\n       </a>\n       :\n       <span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr">\n        <i>\n         Lac \xc3\x89ri\xc3\xa9\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       ) is the fourth-largest\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake" title="Lake">\n        lake\n       </a>\n       (by surface area) of the five\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">\n        Great Lakes\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">\n        North America\n       </a>\n       , and the eleventh-largest globally if measured in terms of surface area.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StateofOhio_1-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-StateofOhio-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldatlas_list_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-worldatlas_list-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is the southernmost, shallowest, and smallest by\n       <a href="/wiki/Volume" title="Volume">\n        volume\n       </a>\n       of the Great Lakes\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GLIN_F.26F_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GLIN_F.26F-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and therefore also has the shortest average water\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_retention_time" title="Lake retention time">\n        residence time\n       </a>\n       . At its deepest point Lake Erie is 210 feet (64 metres) deep.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Situated on the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Boundary" title="International Boundary">\n        International Boundary\n       </a>\n       between Canada and the United States, Lake Erie\'s northern shore is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">\n        Canadian\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">\n        province\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">\n        Ontario\n       </a>\n       , with the\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">\n        U.S. states\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">\n        Michigan\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">\n        Ohio\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">\n        Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">\n        New York\n       </a>\n       on its western, southern and eastern shores. These jurisdictions divide the surface area of the lake with water boundaries.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The lake was named by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Erie_people" title="Erie people">\n        Erie people\n       </a>\n       , a\n       <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">\n        Native Americans\n       </a>\n       people who lived along its southern shore. The tribal name "erie" is a shortened form of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iroquoian" title="Iroquoian">\n        Iroquoian\n       </a>\n       word\n       <i>\n        erielhonan\n       </i>\n       , meaning "long tail".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Room2006_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Room2006-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Situated below\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Huron" title="Lake Huron">\n        Lake Huron\n       </a>\n       , Erie\'s primary inlet is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_River" title="Detroit River">\n        Detroit River\n       </a>\n       . The main natural outflow from the lake is via the\n       <a href="/wiki/Niagara_River" title="Niagara River">\n        Niagara River\n       </a>\n       , which provides\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydroelectric_power" title="Hydroelectric power">\n        hydroelectric power\n       </a>\n       to Canada and the U.S. as it spins huge turbines near\n       <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls" title="Niagara Falls">\n        Niagara Falls\n       </a>\n       at\n       <a href="/wiki/Lewiston_(town),_New_York" title="Lewiston (town), New York">\n        Lewiston, New York\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Queenston,_Ontario" title="Queenston, Ontario">\n        Queenston, Ontario\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ54_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ54-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some outflow occurs via the\n       <a href="/wiki/Welland_Canal" title="Welland Canal">\n        Welland Canal\n       </a>\n       , part of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_Seaway" title="St. Lawrence Seaway">\n        St. Lawrence Seaway\n       </a>\n       , which diverts water for ship passages from\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_Colborne" title="Port Colborne">\n        Port Colborne\n       </a>\n       , Ontario on Lake Erie, to\n       <a href="/wiki/St._Catharines" title="St. Catharines">\n        St. Catharines\n       </a>\n       on\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ontario" title="Lake Ontario">\n        Lake Ontario\n       </a>\n       , an elevation difference of 326\xc2\xa0ft (99\xc2\xa0m). Lake Erie\'s environmental health has been an ongoing concern for decades, with issues such as overfishing,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">\n        pollution\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Algal_bloom" title="Algal bloom">\n        algae blooms\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Eutrophication" title="Eutrophication">\n        eutrophication\n       </a>\n       generating headlines.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ61_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ61-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT031413_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT031413-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX412a_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX412a-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#Geography">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           1\n    <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">\n        Geography\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lake_Erie_NASA.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="711" data-file-width="1278" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Lake_Erie_NASA.jpg/220px-Lake_Erie_NASA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Lake_Erie_NASA.jpg/330px-Lake_Erie_NASA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Lake_Erie_NASA.jpg/440px-Lake_Erie_NASA.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lake_Erie_NASA.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         False-color satellite image of Lake Erie in 2007\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lake_Erie_North_Short_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Lake_Erie_North_Short_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/220px-Lake_Erie_North_Short_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Lake_Erie_North_Short_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/330px-Lake_Erie_North_Short_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 1.5x, class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lake_Erie_North_Short_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Lake Erie: North Shore in mid-December 2014.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geographic_features">\n        Geographic features\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geographic features">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie_Basin" title="Lake Erie Basin">\n        Lake Erie Basin\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Lake Erie (42.2\xc2\xb0 N, 81.2W) has a mean elevation of 571 feet (174\xc2\xa0m)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt_3-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nyt-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       above sea level. It has a surface area of 9,990 square miles (25,874\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       )\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA_2-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EPA-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with a length of 241\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Statute_mile" title="Statute mile">\n        statute miles\n       </a>\n       (388\n       <a href="/wiki/Kilometre" title="Kilometre">\n        km\n       </a>\n       ; 209\n       <a href="/wiki/Nautical_mile" title="Nautical mile">\n        nmi\n       </a>\n       )\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA_2-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EPA-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and breadth of 57 statute miles (92\xc2\xa0km; 50\xc2\xa0nmi)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA_2-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EPA-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       at its widest points.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It is the shallowest of the Great Lakes with an average depth of 10\n       <a href="/wiki/Fathom" title="Fathom">\n        fathoms\n       </a>\n       3 feet (62\xc2\xa0ft (19\xc2\xa0m)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA_2-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EPA-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and a maximum depth of 35 fathoms (210\xc2\xa0ft; 64\xc2\xa0m)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA_2-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EPA-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt_3-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nyt-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For comparison,\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Superior" title="Lake Superior">\n        Lake Superior\n       </a>\n       has an average depth of 80 fathoms 3 feet (483\xc2\xa0ft (147\xc2\xa0m), a volume of 2,900 cubic miles (12,000\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        3\n       </sup>\n       ) and shoreline of 2,726 statute miles (4,385\xc2\xa0km). Because it is the shallowest, it is also the warmest of the Great Lakes,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and in 1999 this almost became a problem for two\n       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_plant" title="Nuclear power plant">\n        nuclear power plants\n       </a>\n       which require cool lake water to keep their reactors cool.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX213_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX213-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The warm summer of 1999 caused lake temperatures to come close to the 85\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (29\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) limit necessary to keep the plants cool.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX213_15-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX213-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Also because of its shallowness, and in spite of being the warmest lake in the summer, it is also the first to freeze in the winter.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The shallowest section of Lake Erie is the western basin where depths average only 25 to 30 feet (7.6 to 9.1\xc2\xa0m); as a result, "the slightest breeze can kick up lively waves," according to a\n       <i>\n        New York Times\n       </i>\n       reporter in 2004.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX43d_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX43d-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The "waves build very quickly", according to other accounts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ31_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ31-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX312c_19-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX312c-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Sometimes fierce waves springing up unexpectedly have led to dramatic rescues; in one instance, a Cleveland resident trying to measure the dock near his house became trapped but was rescued by a fire department diver from\n       <a href="/wiki/Avon_Lake,_Ohio" title="Avon Lake, Ohio">\n        Avon Lake, Ohio\n       </a>\n       :\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        In a tug of war against the waves, the two were finally hauled out by rope. After being trapped for an hour-and-a-half, Baker was back on dry land, exhausted and battered but alive.\n       </p>\n       <div class="templatequotecite">\n        \xe2\x80\x94\n        <cite>\n         Tatiana Morales,\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/CBS_News" title="CBS News">\n           CBS News\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         , 2004\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX411_20-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-twsX411-20">\n           [20]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </cite>\n       </div>\n      </blockquote>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Near_the_Whirlpool,_Niagara_Gorge.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1122" data-file-width="748" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Near_the_Whirlpool%2C_Niagara_Gorge.jpg/170px-Near_the_Whirlpool%2C_Niagara_Gorge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Near_the_Whirlpool%2C_Niagara_Gorge.jpg/255px-Near_the_Whirlpool%2C_Niagara_Gorge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Near_the_Whirlpool%2C_Niagara_Gorge.jpg/340px-Near_the_Whirlpool%2C_Niagara_Gorge.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Near_the_Whirlpool,_Niagara_Gorge.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/Niagara_River" title="Niagara River">\n          Niagara River\n         </a>\n         empties Lake Erie into\n         <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ontario" title="Lake Ontario">\n          Lake Ontario\n         </a>\n         . This water has just passed over\n         <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls" title="Niagara Falls">\n          Niagara Falls\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       This area is also known as the "thunderstorm capital of Canada" with "breathtaking" lightning displays.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX312c_19-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX312c-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Lake Erie is primarily fed by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_River" title="Detroit River">\n        Detroit River\n       </a>\n       (from\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Huron" title="Lake Huron">\n        Lake Huron\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_Saint_Clair_(North_America)" title="Lake Saint Clair (North America)">\n        Lake St. Clair\n       </a>\n       ) and drains via the\n       <a href="/wiki/Niagara_River" title="Niagara River">\n        Niagara River\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls" title="Niagara Falls">\n        Niagara Falls\n       </a>\n       into\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ontario" title="Lake Ontario">\n        Lake Ontario\n       </a>\n       . Navigation downstream is provided by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Welland_Canal" title="Welland Canal">\n        Welland Canal\n       </a>\n       , part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_Seaway" title="Saint Lawrence Seaway">\n        Saint Lawrence Seaway\n       </a>\n       . Other major contributors to Lake Erie include the\n       <a href="/wiki/Grand_River_(Ontario)" title="Grand River (Ontario)">\n        Grand River\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Huron_River_(Michigan)" title="Huron River (Michigan)">\n        Huron River\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Maumee_River" title="Maumee River">\n        Maumee River\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sandusky_River" title="Sandusky River">\n        Sandusky River\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_River_(New_York)" title="Buffalo River (New York)">\n        Buffalo River\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cuyahoga_River" title="Cuyahoga River">\n        Cuyahoga River\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">\n        drainage basin\n       </a>\n       covers 30,140 square miles (78,100\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Point_Pelee_National_Park" title="Point Pelee National Park">\n        Point Pelee National Park\n       </a>\n       , the southernmost point of the Canadian mainland, is located on a peninsula extending into the lake. Several islands are found in the western end of the lake; these belong to Ohio except for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pelee_Island" title="Pelee Island">\n        Pelee Island\n       </a>\n       and eight neighboring islands, which are part of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ontario,_Canada" title="Ontario, Canada">\n        Ontario\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Major cities along Lake Erie include\n       <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">\n        Buffalo\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/Erie,_Pennsylvania" title="Erie, Pennsylvania">\n        Erie, Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Ohio" title="Toledo, Ohio">\n        Toledo, Ohio\n       </a>\n       ; and\n       <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">\n        Cleveland, Ohio\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bass_Islands_map.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="990" data-file-width="800" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Bass_Islands_map.png/170px-Bass_Islands_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Bass_Islands_map.png/255px-Bass_Islands_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Bass_Islands_map.png/340px-Bass_Islands_map.png 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bass_Islands_map.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Partial map of the\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_Erie_Islands" title="Lake Erie Islands">\n          Lake Erie Islands\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Islands">\n        Islands\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Islands">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_Erie_Islands" title="Lake Erie Islands">\n        Lake Erie Islands\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Islands tend to be located in the western side of the lake and total 31 in number (13 in Canada, 18 in the U.S.). The island-village of\n       <a href="/wiki/Put-in-Bay,_Ohio" title="Put-in-Bay, Ohio">\n        Put-in-Bay\n       </a>\n       on\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Bass_Island" title="South Bass Island">\n        South Bass Island\n       </a>\n       attracts young crowds who sometimes wear "red bucket hats" and are prone to "break off cartwheels in the park" and general merriment.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX21a_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX21a-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Kelleys_Island,_Ohio" title="Kelleys Island, Ohio">\n        Kelleys Island\n       </a>\n       was depicted by the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Tribune" title="Chicago Tribune">\n         Chicago Tribune\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       as having charms that were "more subtle" than Put-in-Bay, and offers amenities such as beach lounging, hiking, biking and "marveling at deep glacial grooves left in limestone."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX21a_21-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX21a-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Pelee,_Ontario" title="Pelee, Ontario">\n        Pelee Island\n       </a>\n       is the largest of Erie\'s islands, accessible by ferry from\n       <a href="/wiki/Leamington,_Ontario" title="Leamington, Ontario">\n        Leamington, Ontario\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Sandusky,_Ohio" title="Sandusky, Ohio">\n        Sandusky, Ohio\n       </a>\n       . The island has a "fragile and unique ecosystem" with plants rarely found in Canada, such as wild hyacinth, yellow horse gentian (\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Triosteum_angustifolium" title="Triosteum angustifolium">\n         Triosteum angustifolium\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ) and prickly pear cactus, as well as two endangered snakes, the blue racer and the Lake Erie water snake. Songbirds migrate to Pelee in spring, and monarch butterflies stop over during the fall.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX18_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX18-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Water_levels">\n        Water levels\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Water levels">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Lake Erie has a\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_retention_time" title="Lake retention time">\n        lake retention time\n       </a>\n       of 2.6 years,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX314a_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX314a-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the shortest of all the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">\n        Great Lakes\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA_Basic_24-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EPA_Basic-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The lake\'s surface area is 9,910 square miles (25,667\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA_2-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EPA-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY112_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY112-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Lake Erie\'s water level fluctuates with the seasons as in the other Great Lakes. Generally, the lowest levels are in January and February, and the highest in June or July, although there have been exceptions. The average yearly level varies depending on long-term precipitation. Short-term level changes are often caused by\n       <a href="/wiki/Seiche" title="Seiche">\n        seiches\n       </a>\n       that are particularly high when southwesterly winds blow across the length of the lake during storms. These cause water to pile up at the eastern end of the lake. Storm-driven seiches can cause damage onshore. During one storm in November 2003, the water level at Buffalo rose by 7 feet (2.1\xc2\xa0m) with waves of 10\xe2\x80\x9315 feet (3.0\xe2\x80\x934.6 metres) for a rise of 22 feet (6.7\xc2\xa0m).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Meanwhile, at the western end of the lake,\n       <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Ohio" title="Toledo, Ohio">\n        Toledo\n       </a>\n       experienced a similar drop in water level. Lake water is used for drinking purposes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX215cc_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX215cc-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Historic High Water\n        </b>\n        . The lake fluctuates from month to month with the highest lake levels in June and July. In the summer of 1986, Lake Erie reached its highest level at 5.08 feet (1.55\xc2\xa0m) above datum.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-COE-2009_28-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-COE-2009-28">\n          [28]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        The high water records were set from 1986 (April) through January 1987. Levels ranged from 4.33\xc2\xa0to 5.08 feet (1.32\xe2\x80\x931.55\xc2\xa0m) above Chart Datum.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-COE-2009_28-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-COE-2009-28">\n          [28]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Historic Low Water\n        </b>\n        . Lake Erie experiences its lowest levels in the winter. In the winter of 1934, Lake Erie reached its lowest level at 1.5 feet (0.46\xc2\xa0m) below datum.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-COE-2009_28-2">\n         <a href="#cite_note-COE-2009-28">\n          [28]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Monthly low water records were set from July 1934 through June 1935. During this twelve-month period water levels ranged from 1.5 feet (0.46\xc2\xa0m) to the Chart Datum.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-COE-2009_28-3">\n         <a href="#cite_note-COE-2009-28">\n          [28]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">\n        Geology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lake_Erie_Land%27s_End.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2989" data-file-width="2904" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Lake_Erie_Land%27s_End.jpg/170px-Lake_Erie_Land%27s_End.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Lake_Erie_Land%27s_End.jpg/255px-Lake_Erie_Land%27s_End.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Lake_Erie_Land%27s_End.jpg/340px-Lake_Erie_Land%27s_End.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lake_Erie_Land%27s_End.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Sandy bluffs along Lake Erie in\n         <a href="/wiki/Erie_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Erie County, Pennsylvania">\n          Erie County, Pennsylvania\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lake_Erie_and_Lake_Saint_Clair_bathymetry_map.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="684" data-file-width="1024" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Lake_Erie_and_Lake_Saint_Clair_bathymetry_map.png/170px-Lake_Erie_and_Lake_Saint_Clair_bathymetry_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Lake_Erie_and_Lake_Saint_Clair_bathymetry_map.png/255px-Lake_Erie_and_Lake_Saint_Clair_bathymetry_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Lake_Erie_and_Lake_Saint_Clair_bathymetry_map.png/340px-Lake_Erie_and_Lake_Saint_Clair_bathymetry_map.png 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lake_Erie_and_Lake_Saint_Clair_bathymetry_map.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Lake Erie and\n         <a href="/wiki/Lake_St._Clair" title="Lake St. Clair">\n          Lake Saint Clair\n         </a>\n         <a href="/wiki/Bathymetry" title="Bathymetry">\n          bathymetric\n         </a>\n         map.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GLBathEr_29-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-GLBathEr-29">\n           [29]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GLBathHur_30-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-GLBathHur-30">\n           [30]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GLBathOnt_31-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-GLBathOnt-31">\n           [31]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GLOBE_32-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-GLOBE-32">\n           [32]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         The deepest point is marked with "\xc3\x97".\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_GLERL_33-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-NOAA_GLERL-33">\n           [33]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Lake Erie was carved out by glacier ice,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StateofOhio_1-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-StateofOhio-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and in its current form is less than 4,000 years old, which is a short span in geological terms. Before this, the land on which the lake now sits went through several complex stages. A large lowland basin formed over two million years ago as a result of an eastern flowing river that existed well before the\n       <a href="/wiki/Quaternary_glaciation" title="Quaternary glaciation">\n        Pleistocene ice ages\n       </a>\n       . This ancient drainage system was destroyed by the first major\n       <a href="/wiki/Glacier" title="Glacier">\n        glacier\n       </a>\n       in the area, while it deepened and enlarged the lowland areas, allowing water to settle and form a lake. The glaciers were able to carve away more land on the eastern side of the lowland because the bedrock is made of shale which is softer than the carbonate rocks of\n       <a href="/wiki/Dolomite" title="Dolomite">\n        dolomite\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">\n        limestone\n       </a>\n       on the western side. Thus, the eastern and central basins of the modern lake are much deeper than the western basin, which averages only 25 feet (7.6\xc2\xa0m) deep and is rich in nutrients and fish.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsOhioStateUniv_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsOhioStateUniv-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Lake Erie is the shallowest of the Great Lakes because the ice was relatively thin and lacked erosion power when it reached that far south, according to one view.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As many as three glaciers advanced and retreated over the land causing temporary lakes to form in the time periods in between each of them. Because each lake had a different volume of water their shorelines rested at differing elevations. The last of these lakes to form,\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Warren" title="Lake Warren">\n        Lake Warren\n       </a>\n       , existed between about 13,000 and 12,000 years ago. It was deeper than the current Lake Erie, so its shoreline existed about eight miles (13\xc2\xa0km) inland from the modern one. The shorelines of these lakes left behind high ground sand ridges that cut through swamps and were used as trails for Indians and later, pioneers. These trails became primitive roads which were eventually paved.\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_30" title="U.S. Route 30">\n        U.S. Route 30\n       </a>\n       west of Delphos and\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_20" title="U.S. Route 20">\n        U.S. Route 20\n       </a>\n       west of Norwalk and east of Cleveland were formed in this manner. One can still see some of these ancient sand dunes that formed in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Oak_Openings_Region" title="Oak Openings Region">\n        Oak Openings Region\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northwestern_Ohio" title="Northwestern Ohio">\n        Northwestern Ohio\n       </a>\n       . There, the sandy dry lake bed soil was not enough to support large trees with the exception of a few species of oaks, forming a rare\n       <a href="/wiki/Oak_savanna" title="Oak savanna">\n        oak savanna\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Native_Americans">\n        Native Americans\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Native Americans">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       At the time of European contact, there were several groups of Indian cultures living around the shores of the eastern end of the lake. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Erie_tribe" title="Erie tribe">\n        Erie tribe\n       </a>\n       (from whom the lake takes its name) lived along the southern edge, while the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neutrals" title="Neutrals">\n        Neutrals\n       </a>\n       (also known as Attawandaron) lived along the northern shore. Near Port Stanley, there is an Indian village dating from the 16th century known as the\n       <i>\n        Southwold Earthworks\n       </i>\n       where as many as 800 Neutral Indians once lived; the archaeological remains include double earth walls winding around the grass-covered perimeter.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX18_22-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX18-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Europeans named the tribe the\n       <i>\n        Neutral Indians\n       </i>\n       since these people refused to fight with other tribes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX18_22-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX18-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Both tribes were conquered and assimilated by their hostile eastern neighbors, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Iroquois" title="Iroquois">\n        Iroquois Confederacy\n       </a>\n       between\n       <a href="/wiki/Anno_Domini" title="Anno Domini">\n        AD\n       </a>\n       1651 and 1657, in what is referred to as part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Beaver_Wars" title="Beaver Wars">\n        Beaver Wars\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For decades after those wars, the land around eastern Lake Erie was claimed and utilized by the Iroquois as a hunting ground. As the power of the Iroquois waned during the last quarter of the 17th century, several other, mainly\n       <a href="/wiki/Anishinaabe" title="Anishinaabe">\n        Anishinaabe\n       </a>\n       Native American tribes, displaced them from the territories they claimed on the north shore of the lake.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There was a legend of an Indian woman named Huldah who, despairing over her lost British lover, hurled herself from a high rock from Pelee Island.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ31_18-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ31-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="European_exploration_and_settlement">\n        European exploration and settlement\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: European exploration and settlement">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Great_Lakes_Steamship_Walk-in-the-Water.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="326" data-file-width="472" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Great_Lakes_Steamship_Walk-in-the-Water.jpg/220px-Great_Lakes_Steamship_Walk-in-the-Water.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Great_Lakes_Steamship_Walk-in-the-Water.jpg/330px-Great_Lakes_Steamship_Walk-in-the-Water.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Great_Lakes_Steamship_Walk-in-the-Water.jpg/440px-Great_Lakes_Steamship_Walk-in-the-Water.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Great_Lakes_Steamship_Walk-in-the-Water.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The steamship\n         <i>\n          Walk in Water\n         </i>\n         , built in Buffalo, was the first steamship on Lake Erie. Picture circa 1816.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 1669, the Frenchman\n       <a href="/wiki/Louis_Jolliet" title="Louis Jolliet">\n        Louis Jolliet\n       </a>\n       was the first documented European to sight Lake Erie, although there is speculation that\n       <a href="/wiki/%C3%89tienne_Br%C3%BBl%C3%A9" title="\xc3\x89tienne Br\xc3\xbbl\xc3\xa9">\n        \xc3\x89tienne Br\xc3\xbbl\xc3\xa9\n       </a>\n       may have come across it in 1615.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Lake Erie was the last of the Great Lakes to be explored by Europeans, since the Iroquois who occupied the\n       <a href="/wiki/Niagara_River" title="Niagara River">\n        Niagara River\n       </a>\n       area were in conflict with the French, and they did not allow explorers or traders to pass through. Explorers followed rivers out of\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ontario" title="Lake Ontario">\n        Lake Ontario\n       </a>\n       and portaged directly into\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Huron" title="Lake Huron">\n        Lake Huron\n       </a>\n       . British authorities in Canada were nervous about possible expansion by American settlers across Lake Erie, so Colonel Talbot developed the Talbot Trail in 1809 as a way to stimulate settlement to the area; Talbot recruited settlers from\n       <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">\n        Ireland\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">\n        Scotland\n       </a>\n       and there are numerous places named after him, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_Talbot,_Ontario" title="Port Talbot, Ontario">\n        Port Talbot\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Talbot_River_(Ontario)" title="Talbot River (Ontario)">\n        Talbot River\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Talbotville,_Ontario" title="Talbotville, Ontario">\n        Talbotville\n       </a>\n       in southern Ontario.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX18_22-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX18-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_erie.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="379" data-file-width="610" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Battle_erie.jpg/220px-Battle_erie.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Battle_erie.jpg/330px-Battle_erie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Battle_erie.jpg/440px-Battle_erie.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_erie.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Hazard_Perry" title="Oliver Hazard Perry">\n          Commander Perry\n         </a>\n         \'s message after the\n         <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lake_Erie" title="Battle of Lake Erie">\n          Battle of Lake Erie\n         </a>\n         : "We have met the enemy and they are ours." This 1865 painting by\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_H._Powell" title="William H. Powell">\n          William H. Powell\n         </a>\n         shows Perry transferring to a different ship during the battle.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       During the\n       <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">\n        War of 1812\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Hazard_Perry" title="Oliver Hazard Perry">\n        Oliver Hazard Perry\n       </a>\n       captured an entire\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lake_Erie" title="Battle of Lake Erie">\n        British fleet\n       </a>\n       in 1813\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ41a_39-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ41a-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       near Put-in-Bay, Ohio, despite having inferior numbers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ16_40-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ16-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       American soldiers swept through the Ontario area around\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_Rowan,_Ontario" title="Port Rowan, Ontario">\n        Port Rowan\n       </a>\n       burning towns and villages, but spared a gristmill owned by a Canadian mason named John Backhouse, according to one report.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX18_22-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX18-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Generally, however, despite the two exceptions being the American Revolutionary War and the War of 1812 which involved conflicts between the U.S. and\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">\n        Great Britain\n       </a>\n       , relations between the U.S. and Canada have been remarkably friendly with an "unfortified boundary" and an agreement "that has kept all fleets of war off the Great Lakes."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ21bb_41-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ21bb-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1837, rebellions broke about between Canadian settlers and the\n       <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">\n        British Colonial government\n       </a>\n       , primarily over political reforms and land allocation issues. Some of the rebels stationed themselves in the U.S. and crossed the ice from Sandusky Bay to Pelee Island wearing "tattered overcoats and worn-out boots", and carrying muskets, pitchforks, and swords,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ31_18-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ31-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but the islanders had already fled.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ31_18-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ31-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Later, there was a battle on the ice with the Royal 32nd regiment, with the rebels being driven to retreat.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ31_18-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ31-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brig_Niagara_(Lorain,_Ohio).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1768" data-file-width="2151" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Brig_Niagara_%28Lorain%2C_Ohio%29.jpg/220px-Brig_Niagara_%28Lorain%2C_Ohio%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Brig_Niagara_%28Lorain%2C_Ohio%29.jpg/330px-Brig_Niagara_%28Lorain%2C_Ohio%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Brig_Niagara_%28Lorain%2C_Ohio%29.jpg/440px-Brig_Niagara_%28Lorain%2C_Ohio%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brig_Niagara_(Lorain,_Ohio).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         At an Ohio history festival, the 19th-century style brig warship USS\n         <i>\n          Niagara\n         </i>\n         passes the\n         <a href="/wiki/Lorain,_Ohio" title="Lorain, Ohio">\n          Lorain\n         </a>\n         lighthouse.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Settlers established commercial fisheries on the north coast of the lake around the 1850s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX14b_42-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX14b-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An important business was fishing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX314a_23-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX314a-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the pre-Civil War years, railways sprouted everywhere, and around 1852 there were railways circling the lake.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ15_43-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ15-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Maritime traffic picked up, although the lake was usually closed because of ice from December to early April, and ships had to wait for the ice to clear before proceeding.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ17_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ17-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Since slavery had been abolished in Canada in 1833, but was still legal in southern states of the U.S., a Lake Erie crossing was sometimes required for fugitive slaves seeking freedom:\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        When Kentucky fugitive Lewis Clarke arrived in Cleveland, he had no idea how to find Canada. "I went out to the shore of the lake again and again, to try and see the other side, but I could see no hill, mountain, nor city of the asylum I sought," he once told an interviewer. "I was afraid to inquire where (Canada) was, lest it would betray such a degree of ignorance as to excite suspicion at once." Many fugitives also had to overcome fears instilled by their former masters...\n       </p>\n       <div class="templatequotecite">\n        \xe2\x80\x94\n        <cite>\n         Chris Lackner in the\n         <i>\n          Ottawa Citizen\n         </i>\n         , 2006\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ51_45-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-twsZ51-45">\n           [45]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </cite>\n       </div>\n      </blockquote>\n      <p>\n       Merchant shippers lacked modern\n       <a href="/wiki/Radar" title="Radar">\n        radar\n       </a>\n       and weather forecasting, so vessels were often caught up in intense gales:\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        A violent gale is blowing on Lake Erie ... The schooner\n        <i>\n         Stranger\n        </i>\n        came in this morning and reports seeing a vessel about 12 miles [19\xc2\xa0km] up, 2 miles [3.2\xc2\xa0km] from the Canada shore, with three men clinging to the masts, which alone were visible above the water\xe2\x80\x93heard their cries and screams...\n       </p>\n       <div class="templatequotecite">\n        \xe2\x80\x94\n        <cite>\n         <i>\n          The New York Times\n         </i>\n         , October 1853\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ11_46-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-twsZ11-46">\n           [46]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </cite>\n       </div>\n      </blockquote>\n      <p>\n       There were reports of disasters usually from sea captains passing information to reporters; in 1868, the captain of the\n       <i>\n        Grace Whitney\n       </i>\n       saw a sunken vessel "three men clinging to the masthead" but he could not help because of the gale and high seas.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ19_47-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ19-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balloonist" title="Balloonist">\n        balloonist\n       </a>\n       named John Steiner of\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">\n        Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       made an ambitious trip across the lake in 1857.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY312_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY312-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       He was described in\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">\n         The New York Times\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       as an\n       <i>\n        eronaut\n       </i>\n       or\n       <i>\n        aeronaut\n       </i>\n       ; powered boats were called\n       <i>\n        propellers\n       </i>\n       ; and fast was deemed\n       <i>\n        railroad speed\n       </i>\n       . Here\'s an account of the day-long voyage over the lake:\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        He arose to the height of about three miles, and started off at a slow but steady rate ... The lake could be seen from one end to the other nearly ... At one time Mr. Steiner counted 38 sail vessels, all in sight, and far below him. The hands on board several of the vessels saw him, and rightly apprehending that he was an aeronaut, cheered him heartily ... He neared the Canada shore a little below Long Point ... he was accordingly driven towards Buffalo ... Night was drawing on and it became apparent that he could not, with this current, get away from the water before dark, and after nightfall it would not be safe to come down. Seeing a propeller ... the\n        <i>\n         Mary Stewart\n        </i>\n        ... He first struck the water about 25 miles below Long Point ... During this time Mr. Steiner says he thinks his balloon bounded from the water at least twenty times. It would strike and then rebound, like a ball, going into the air from twenty to fifty feet, and still rushing down the lake at railroad speed ... Mr. Steiner then abandoned the balloon, leaping into the water and swimming towards the boat, which speedily reached him...\n       </p>\n       <div class="templatequotecite">\n        \xe2\x80\x94\n        <cite>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">\n           The New York Times\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         , July 23, 1857\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY312_48-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY312-48">\n           [48]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </cite>\n       </div>\n      </blockquote>\n      <p>\n       In 1885, lake winds were so strong that water levels dropped substantially, sometimes by as much as two feet, so that at ports such as Toledo, watercraft could not load coal or depart the port.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ22_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ22-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the history of the lake as a\n       <i>\n        fishery\n       </i>\n       , there has been marked battling by opposing interest groups. Here\'s an 1895 newspaper account in which critics of commercial fishing issued dire predictions and calling for government action to solve the problem:\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        The preservation of the fisheries of Lake Erie has become a serious problem to all who have given it close attention ... the fisheries are being exhausted by the wasteful methods which are now in vogue ... it is still the custom of the pound fishermen about Sandusky to take fish of all sizes, and if they are too small to be marketable they are turned over to a fertilizer factory. If left undisturbed for two or three years more, these little fish would be a very valuable product ...\n       </p>\n       <div class="templatequotecite">\n        \xe2\x80\x94\n        <cite>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">\n           The New York Times\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         , 1895\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY314_50-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY314-50">\n           [50]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </cite>\n       </div>\n      </blockquote>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Put-in-Bay_view_from_the_Peace_Memorial.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Put-in-Bay_view_from_the_Peace_Memorial.jpg/220px-Put-in-Bay_view_from_the_Peace_Memorial.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Put-in-Bay_view_from_the_Peace_Memorial.jpg/330px-Put-in-Bay_view_from_the_Peace_Memorial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Put-in-Bay_view_from_the_Peace_Memorial.jpg/440px-Put-in-Bay_view_from_the_Peace_Memorial.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Put-in-Bay_view_from_the_Peace_Memorial.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         View from the\n         <a href="/wiki/Perry%27s_Victory_and_International_Peace_Memorial" title="Perry\'s Victory and International Peace Memorial">\n          Peace Memorial\n         </a>\n         at\n         <a href="/wiki/Put-in-Bay,_Ohio" title="Put-in-Bay, Ohio">\n          Put-in-Bay, Ohio\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Predictions of the lake being over-fished in 1895 were premature, since the fishery has survived commercial and sport fishing, pollution in the middle of the 20th century, invasive species and other ailments, but state and provincial governments, as well as national governments, have played a greater role as time went by. Business boomed; in 1901, the Carnegie Company proposed building a new harbor near\n       <a href="/wiki/Erie,_Pennsylvania" title="Erie, Pennsylvania">\n        Erie\n       </a>\n       in Elk Creek to accommodate shipments from its tube-plant site nearby.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ18_51-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ18-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1913, a memorial to Commodore Perry was built on Put-in-Bay island featuring a Doric column.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ21bb_41-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ21bb-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the\n       <a href="/wiki/Prohibition_in_the_United_States" title="Prohibition in the United States">\n        Prohibition\n       </a>\n       years from 1919 to 1933, a "great deal of alcohol crossed Erie"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ31_18-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ31-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       along with "mobster corpses" dumped into the\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_River" title="Detroit River">\n        Detroit River\n       </a>\n       which sometimes washed up on the beaches of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pelee_Island" title="Pelee Island">\n        Pelee Island\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX312a_52-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX312a-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       According to one account,\n       <a href="/wiki/Al_Capone" title="Al Capone">\n        Al Capone\n       </a>\n       hid a "fortune" in the walls of the Middle Island luxury club, but no money was found in it as of 2007 when the building no longer stood.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ31_18-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ31-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The club had a basement casino with poker tables and slot machines.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ31_18-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ31-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the 20th century, commercial fishing was prevalent, but so was the boom in manufacturing industry around the lake, and often rivers and streams were used as sewers to flush untreated sewage which ended up in the lake.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY214a_53-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY214a-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Sometimes poorly constructed sanitary systems meant that when old mains broke, raw sewage would spill directly into the Cuyahoga and into the lake.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY214a_53-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY214a-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A report in\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">\n         Time\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       magazine in 1969 described the lake as a "gigantic cesspool" since only three of 62 beaches were rated "completely safe for swimming".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY214a_53-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY214a-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       By 1975 the popular commercial fish\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue_pike" title="Blue pike">\n        blue pike\n       </a>\n       had been declared extinct, although the declaration may have been premature.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX512_54-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX512-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By the 1980s, there were about 130 fishing vessels with about 3,000 workers,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX14b_42-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX14b-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but commercial fishing was declining rapidly, particularly from the American side.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Great_Lakes_Compact">\n        Great Lakes Compact\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Great Lakes Compact">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_Compact" title="Great Lakes Compact">\n        Great Lakes Compact\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 2005, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">\n        Great Lakes\n       </a>\n       States of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">\n        Ohio\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">\n        Michigan\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">\n        New York\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">\n        Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">\n        Illinois\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">\n        Indiana\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">\n        Wisconsin\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">\n        Minnesota\n       </a>\n       and the Canadian Provinces of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">\n        Ontario\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">\n        Quebec\n       </a>\n       endorsed the Great Lakes-St. Lawrence River Basin Sustainable Water Resources Compact (Compact). The Compact was signed into law by President\n       <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">\n        George W. Bush\n       </a>\n       in September 2008. An international water rights policy overseen by the Great Lakes Commission, the Compact aims to prevent diversion of water from Great Lakes to distant states, as well as to set standards for use and conservation. It had support from both political parties, including former United States Senator\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Voinovich" title="George Voinovich">\n        George Voinovich\n       </a>\n       (R-OH) and former Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Granholm" title="Jennifer Granholm">\n        Jennifer Granholm\n       </a>\n       (D-MI), but is not popular in the southwestern states due to frequent drought conditions and\n       <a href="/wiki/Water_scarcity" title="Water scarcity">\n        water scarcity\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Lake_environment">\n        Lake environment\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Lake environment">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Weather">\n        Weather\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Weather">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Lake_Erie_in_winter">\n        Lake Erie in winter\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Lake Erie in winter">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LakeEffectSnow.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="800" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/LakeEffectSnow.png/220px-LakeEffectSnow.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/LakeEffectSnow.png/330px-LakeEffectSnow.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/LakeEffectSnow.png/440px-LakeEffectSnow.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LakeEffectSnow.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Cold air travels over warm lake water. The air becomes warmer, moister, less dense, so that it rises; when it passes over land, the reduced airspace causes the air to "pile up" resulting in "frictional convergence." This lifts the air even further to where it cools, turning into droplets or snowflakes. The result is enhanced snowfall.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY313b_55-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY313b-55">\n           [55]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Erie_Michigan_1953_tornado.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="536" data-file-width="800" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Erie_Michigan_1953_tornado.jpg/220px-Erie_Michigan_1953_tornado.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Erie_Michigan_1953_tornado.jpg/330px-Erie_Michigan_1953_tornado.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Erie_Michigan_1953_tornado.jpg/440px-Erie_Michigan_1953_tornado.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Erie_Michigan_1953_tornado.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Tornadoes rarely happen around the immediate Great Lakes region, although this one happened in 1953 in Erie, Michigan near Lake Erie.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LakeErie-1.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="384" data-file-width="512" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/LakeErie-1.jpg/220px-LakeErie-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/LakeErie-1.jpg/330px-LakeErie-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/LakeErie-1.jpg/440px-LakeErie-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LakeErie-1.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Lake Erie in winter\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Like the other Great Lakes, Erie produces\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_effect_snow" title="Lake effect snow">\n        lake effect snow\n       </a>\n       when the first cold winds of winter pass over the warm waters. When the difference in temperature between the relatively warm surface water and the colder air reaches a threshold value of 18 to 23 degrees Fahrenheit (10 to 13 degrees Celsius), then "lake-effect snow becomes possible:"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY313b_55-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY313b-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        As cold air flows over the warm water, the lake warms and moistens the air. Since warm, moist air is less dense than cold air, the heated air rises. Rising air cools and water vapor condenses into cloud droplets ... the efficiency of snow production increases when the wind pushes the clouds over land. Friction with the ground causes air to pile up. This frictional convergence creates lift and enhances snowfall.\n       </p>\n       <div class="templatequotecite">\n        \xe2\x80\x94\n        <cite>\n         Bob Swanson and Adrienne Lewis of\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">\n           USA Today\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         , 2008\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY313b_55-2">\n          <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY313b-55">\n           [55]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </cite>\n       </div>\n      </blockquote>\n      <p>\n       Heavy lake-effect snowfalls can occur when cold air travels 60 miles (97\xc2\xa0km) or longer over a large unfrozen lake.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY313b_55-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY313b-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Lake-effect snow makes\n       <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">\n        Buffalo\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Erie,_Pennsylvania" title="Erie, Pennsylvania">\n        Erie\n       </a>\n       the eleventh and thirteenth snowiest places in the entire\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       respectively, according to data collected from the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Climatic_Data_Center" title="National Climatic Data Center">\n        National Climatic Data Center\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Since winds blow primarily west\xe2\x80\x93to\xe2\x80\x93east along the main axis of the lake, lake effect snow effects are more pronounced on the eastern parts of the lake such as cities such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">\n        Buffalo\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Erie,_Pennsylvania" title="Erie, Pennsylvania">\n        Erie\n       </a>\n       . Buffalo typically gets 95 inches (240\xc2\xa0cm) of snow each winter, and sometimes ten feet (3.0\xc2\xa0m) of snow;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY313a_57-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY313a-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the snowiest city is\n       <a href="/wiki/Syracuse,_New_York" title="Syracuse, New York">\n        Syracuse, New York\n       </a>\n       , which can receive heavy snowfall from both the lake effect process and large coastal cyclones. A storm around Christmas in 2001 pounded Buffalo with seven feet of snow.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY111_58-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY111-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Frozen_Lake_Erie.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="560" data-file-width="1945" height="63" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Frozen_Lake_Erie.jpg/220px-Frozen_Lake_Erie.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Frozen_Lake_Erie.jpg/330px-Frozen_Lake_Erie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Frozen_Lake_Erie.jpg/440px-Frozen_Lake_Erie.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Frozen_Lake_Erie.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Lake Erie in winter\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The lake effect ends or its effect is reduced, however, when the lake freezes over. In January 2011, for example, residents of Cleveland were glad when Lake Erie was "90 percent frozen" since it meant that the area had "made it over the hump" in terms of enduring repeated snowfalls which required much shoveling.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX211_59-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX211-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Being the shallowest of the Great Lakes, it is the most likely to freeze and frequently does.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Straight_Dope_60-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Straight_Dope-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On February 16, 2010, meteorologists reported that the lake had frozen over marking the first time the lake had completely frozen over since the winter of 1995\xe2\x80\x931996.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In contrast,\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Michigan" title="Lake Michigan">\n        Lake Michigan\n       </a>\n       has never completely frozen over since the warmer and deeper portion is in the south, although it came close to being totally frozen during three harsh winters over the past century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX35_62-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX35-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       When the lake freezes over, this usually shuts down the lake effect snowfall.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX36_63-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX36-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In past years, lake ice was so thick that it was possible to drive over it or go sailing on iceboats; but in the first decade of the 21st century, the ice has not been thick enough for such activities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX312a_52-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX312a-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Many lake residents take advantage of the ice and travel; some drive to Canada and back.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY114_64-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY114-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Here\'s one account of ice life around Put-in-Bay:\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        The first ice usually forms in late November, and by January it locks into place. For islanders in the Western Basin, it is the equivalent of summer vacation ... Once the lake freezes, islanders organize impromptu ice rallies. Families gather to drink hot wine and race all-terrain vehicles across the lake. They also race\n        <a href="/wiki/Ice_boat" title="Ice boat">\n         iceboats\n        </a>\n        , which resemble sailboats on skates ... Many people drive to other islands for dinner with friends. They ride in cars with the roofs and doors chopped off so they can escape if the vehicles fall through the ice. Islanders stab evergreen trees into the ice every 50 yards to mark a route ... Even in the coldest winters, there are dangerous patches of thin ice. The cracks are so predictable that the Put-in-Bay Ice Yacht Club prints them on a map ...
