On a normal winter day, the ice is dotted with 2,000 fishing shanties.\n       </p>\n       <div class="templatequotecite">\n        \xe2\x80\x94\n        <cite>\n         Christopher Maag in\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">\n           The New York Times\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         , 2004\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY114_64-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY114-64">\n           [64]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </cite>\n       </div>\n      </blockquote>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Windy_conditions">\n        Windy conditions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Windy conditions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Strong winds have caused lake currents to shift sediment on the bottom, leading to "wickedly shifting sandbars" which have been a source of shipwrecks.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX312a_52-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX312a-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       But winds can have a peaceful purpose as well; there have been proposals to place electricity\xe2\x80\x93producing\n       <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine" title="Wind turbine">\n        wind turbines\n       </a>\n       in windy and shallow points in the lake and along the coast, both in the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">\n        Canada\n       </a>\n       . In 2010, there were plans for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Electric_Corporation" title="General Electric Corporation">\n        GE\n       </a>\n       to develop five wind turbines to generate 20 megawatts of power by 2012 with plans to generate 1,000 megawatts by 2020; one proposal called for "gearless turbines" with 176-foot long blades helped along with magnets.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY215_65-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY215-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX11_66-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX11-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A nonprofit development group near Cleveland was developing plans to construct hundreds of turbines in the lake.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY213_67-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY213-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A former steel mill site on the eastern edge of the lake in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buffalo,_NY" title="Buffalo, NY">\n        Buffalo, NY\n       </a>\n       has been redeveloped as an urban wind farm in 2007. Known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Steel_Winds" title="Steel Winds">\n        Steel Winds\n       </a>\n       , the project currently houses 14 turbines capable of generating up to 35 megawatts of electricity.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A plan by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samsung_Corporation" title="Samsung Corporation">\n        Samsung\n       </a>\n       to build an offshore\n       <a href="/wiki/Wind_farm" title="Wind farm">\n        wind farm\n       </a>\n       on the north shore of the lake, from\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_Maitland,_Ontario" title="Port Maitland, Ontario">\n        Port Maitland\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Nanticoke,_Ontario" title="Nanticoke, Ontario">\n        Nanticoke\n       </a>\n       for a distance of 15.5\xc2\xa0mi (24.9\xc2\xa0km),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY113_69-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY113-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but the plan has been met with opposition from residents for a number of reasons. Canadians near\n       <a href="/wiki/Leamington,_Ontario" title="Leamington, Ontario">\n        Leamington\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Kingsville,_Ontario" title="Kingsville, Ontario">\n        Kingsville\n       </a>\n       have organized protest groups to thwart attempts to bring wind turbines to the lake; reasons against the turbines include spoiling lake views as well as possible adverse effects regarding drinking water and commercial fishing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ24_70-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ24-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Plans to install turbines in Pigeon Bay, south of\n       <a href="/wiki/Leamington,_Ontario" title="Leamington, Ontario">\n        Leamington\n       </a>\n       were met with opposition as well.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ56_71-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ56-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ55_72-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ55-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The notion that bird and bat migration may be hurt by the wind turbines has been used to argue against the wind turbines; a reporter in\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Globe_and_Mail" title="The Globe and Mail">\n         The Globe and Mail\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       wrote "Given the tendency of turbines to make mincemeat of things airborne, it doesn\xe2\x80\x99t require great imagination to figure out what would happen."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ24_70-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ24-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        They loom like gigantic aliens invading the farmers\xe2\x80\x99 fields. There are 66 of these creatures, each about as tall as a 25-storey building with a face comprised of three enormous whiskers rotating 11 to 20 times per minute. Standing amidst the wind turbines of Erie Shore Wind Farm, one feels like a doomed character in a sci-fi movie caught in the deathly still moment just before disaster strikes.\n       </p>\n       <div class="templatequotecite">\n        \xe2\x80\x94\n        <cite>\n         reporter Rebecca Field Jager in the\n         <i>\n          Weekend Post\n         </i>\n         , 2010\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ35b_73-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-twsZ35b-73">\n           [73]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </cite>\n       </div>\n      </blockquote>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Microclimates">\n        Microclimates\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Microclimates">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The lake is also responsible for\n       <a href="/wiki/Microclimate" title="Microclimate">\n        microclimates\n       </a>\n       that are important to\n       <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">\n        agriculture\n       </a>\n       . Along its north shore is one of the richest areas of Canada\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">\n        fruit\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Vegetable" title="Vegetable">\n        vegetable\n       </a>\n       production; this southernmost tip, particularly in the area around Leamington, is known as Canada\'s "tomato capital".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ24_70-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ24-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The area around\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_Rowan,_Ontario" title="Port Rowan, Ontario">\n        Port Rowan\n       </a>\n       in Ontario has special trees which grow because of the "tempering effect of the lake", and species include tulip trees, flowering dogwood, sassafras and sour gum.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX18_22-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX18-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In this area there are many greenhouses which produce a "variety of tropical plants rarely cultivated so far north", including some species of\n       <a href="/wiki/Cactus" title="Cactus">\n        cacti\n       </a>\n       , because of the lake\'s tempering effect.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX18_22-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX18-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Along the southeastern shore in Ohio, Pennsylvania, and New York is an important\n       <a href="/wiki/Grape" title="Grape">\n        grape\n       </a>\n       growing region, as are the islands in the lake.\n       <a href="/wiki/Apple" title="Apple">\n        Apple\n       </a>\n       orchards are abundant in northeast Ohio to western New York.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Long_term_weather_patterns">\n        Long term weather patterns\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Long term weather patterns">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       According to one estimate, 34 to 36 inches of water evaporates each year from the surface of the lake,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StateofOhio_1-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-StateofOhio-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which allows for rainfall and other precipitation in surrounding areas. There are conflicting reports about the overall effect of\n       <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">\n        global warming\n       </a>\n       on the Great Lakes region\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="Section talks about controversy in two spots, but does not identify any sort of controversy. (June 2014)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       , including Lake Erie. One account suggests that climate change is causing greater\n       <a href="/wiki/Evaporation" title="Evaporation">\n        evaporation\n       </a>\n       of lake water, leading to warmer temperatures as well as ice in winter which is less thick or nonexistent, fueling concerns that "Erie appears to be shrinking" and is the most likely candidate among the five Great Lakes to "turn into a festering mud puddle."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX312a_52-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX312a-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2010, the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Windsor_Star" title="Windsor Star">\n         Windsor Star\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       reported that the lake experienced "record-breaking temperatures" reaching 81\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (27\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) in mid-August and compared the lake to a "bath tub".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ27_74-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ27-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       But the long term weather patterns are subject to controversy.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="Section talks about controversy in two spots, but does not identify any sort of controversy. (June 2014)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ecosystems">\n        Ecosystems\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Ecosystems">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Avon_Lake_power_plant.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Avon_Lake_power_plant.jpg/220px-Avon_Lake_power_plant.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Avon_Lake_power_plant.jpg/330px-Avon_Lake_power_plant.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Avon_Lake_power_plant.jpg/440px-Avon_Lake_power_plant.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Avon_Lake_power_plant.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A\n         <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_power_station" title="Fossil fuel power station">\n          coal-fired power plant\n         </a>\n         in\n         <a href="/wiki/Avon_Lake,_Ohio" title="Avon Lake, Ohio">\n          Avon Lake, Ohio\n         </a>\n         located on Lake Erie\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Lake Erie has a complex ecosystem with many species in constant interaction. Human activity, such as pollution and maritime ship traffic, can affect this environment in numerous ways. The interactions between the new species can sometimes have beneficial effects, as well as harmful effects. Some introductions have been seen as beneficial such as the introduction of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_salmon" title="Pacific salmon">\n        Pacific salmon\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX312a_52-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX312a-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Occasionally there have been mass die-offs of certain species of fish, sometimes for reasons unknown, such as many numbers of\n       <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_smelt" title="Rainbow smelt">\n        rainbow smelt\n       </a>\n       in May 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ_75-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Invasive_species">\n        Invasive species\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Invasive species">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The lake has been plagued with a number of\n       <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">\n        invasive species\n       </a>\n       , including\n       <a href="/wiki/Zebra_mussel" title="Zebra mussel">\n        zebra\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX312a_52-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX312a-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Quagga_mussel" title="Quagga mussel">\n        quagga\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Mussel" title="Mussel">\n        mussels\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Round_goby" title="Round goby">\n        goby\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Grass_carp" title="Grass carp">\n        grass carp\n       </a>\n       . One estimate was that there have been 180 invasive species in the Great Lakes, some having traveled in ballast water in international ships.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ28a_76-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ28a-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Zebra mussels and gobies have been credited with the increased population and size of\n       <a href="/wiki/Smallmouth_bass" title="Smallmouth bass">\n        smallmouth bass\n       </a>\n       in Lake Erie.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n        <a href="#cite_note-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2008 there were concerns that the "newest invader swarming in the Great Lakes", which was the "bloody-red shrimp", might harm fish populations and promote\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algae_bloom" title="Algae bloom">\n        algae blooms\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ45_78-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ45-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Environmentalists and biologists study lake conditions via installations such as the Franz Theodore Stone Laboratory on\n       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Island" title="Gibraltar Island">\n        Gibraltar Island\n       </a>\n       . The lab, which was established in 1895, is the oldest biological field station in the United States. Stone Laboratory was donated to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_University" title="Ohio State University">\n        Ohio State University\n       </a>\n       by Julius Stone in 1925 as part of the university\'s Ohio Sea Grant College Program.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsOhioStateUniv_34-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsOhioStateUniv-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ28a_76-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ28a-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition, the Great Lakes Institute of the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Windsor" title="University of Windsor">\n        University of Windsor\n       </a>\n       has experts who study issues such as lake sediment pollution and the flow of contaminants such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Phosphorus" title="Phosphorus">\n        phosphorus\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ28a_76-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ28a-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A list of the common invasive species in Lake Erie include: Zebra Mussels, Quagga Mussels, Round Gobies, Spiny European Water Fleas, Fishhook Water Fleas, the Sea Lamprey, and White Perch. The invasive plant species that fill Lake Erie consist mainly of Eurasian Milfoil, and Purple Loosestrife,\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Eutrophication_and_the_infamous_dead_zone">\n        Eutrophication and the infamous dead zone\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Eutrophication and the infamous dead zone">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HAZARDOUS_WALK_OFF_HUNTINGTON_BEACH_ON_LAKE_ERIE_THROUGH_ALGAE_AND_UPROOTED_TREES._HIGH_WATER_AND_UNCONTROLLED..._-_NARA_-_550242.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="2028" height="325" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/HAZARDOUS_WALK_OFF_HUNTINGTON_BEACH_ON_LAKE_ERIE_THROUGH_ALGAE_AND_UPROOTED_TREES._HIGH_WATER_AND_UNCONTROLLED..._-_NARA_-_550242.jpg/220px-HAZARDOUS_WALK_OFF_HUNTINGTON_BEACH_ON_LAKE_ERIE_THROUGH_ALGAE_AND_UPROOTED_TREES._HIGH_WATER_AND_UNCONTROLLED..._-_NARA_-_550242.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/HAZARDOUS_WALK_OFF_HUNTINGTON_BEACH_ON_LAKE_ERIE_THROUGH_ALGAE_AND_UPROOTED_TREES._HIGH_WATER_AND_UNCONTROLLED..._-_NARA_-_550242.jpg/330px-HAZARDOUS_WALK_OFF_HUNTINGTON_BEACH_ON_LAKE_ERIE_THROUGH_ALGAE_AND_UPROOTED_TREES._HIGH_WATER_AND_UNCONTROLLED..._-_NARA_-_550242.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/HAZARDOUS_WALK_OFF_HUNTINGTON_BEACH_ON_LAKE_ERIE_THROUGH_ALGAE_AND_UPROOTED_TREES._HIGH_WATER_AND_UNCONTROLLED..._-_NARA_-_550242.jpg/440px-HAZARDOUS_WALK_OFF_HUNTINGTON_BEACH_ON_LAKE_ERIE_THROUGH_ALGAE_AND_UPROOTED_TREES._HIGH_WATER_AND_UNCONTROLLED..._-_NARA_-_550242.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HAZARDOUS_WALK_OFF_HUNTINGTON_BEACH_ON_LAKE_ERIE_THROUGH_ALGAE_AND_UPROOTED_TREES._HIGH_WATER_AND_UNCONTROLLED..._-_NARA_-_550242.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A 1973 photo from the U.S.\n         <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">\n          Environmental Protection Agency\n         </a>\n         showing beach erosion, algae, and uprooted trees as a result of environmental issues\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toxic_Algae_Bloom_in_Lake_Erie.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="5000" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Toxic_Algae_Bloom_in_Lake_Erie.jpg/220px-Toxic_Algae_Bloom_in_Lake_Erie.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Toxic_Algae_Bloom_in_Lake_Erie.jpg/330px-Toxic_Algae_Bloom_in_Lake_Erie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Toxic_Algae_Bloom_in_Lake_Erie.jpg/440px-Toxic_Algae_Bloom_in_Lake_Erie.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toxic_Algae_Bloom_in_Lake_Erie.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The green scum shown in this image taken in October 2011 is the worst\n         <a href="/wiki/Algal_bloom" title="Algal bloom">\n          algae bloom\n         </a>\n         Lake Erie has experienced in decades.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       An ongoing concern is that "nutrient overloading from fertilizers, human and animal waste", known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Eutrophication" title="Eutrophication">\n        eutrophication\n       </a>\n       , in which additional\n       <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">\n        nitrogen\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Phosphorus" title="Phosphorus">\n        phosphorus\n       </a>\n       enter the lake, will cause plant life to "run wild and multiply like crazy".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ61_11-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ61-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Since there are fewer\n       <a href="/wiki/Wetland" title="Wetland">\n        wetlands\n       </a>\n       , which are like "Nature\'s kidneys" by filtering nutrients, as well as greater "channelization of waterways", nutrients in water can cause algal blooms to sprout as well as "low-oxygen dead zones" in a complex interaction of natural forces.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ61_11-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ61-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As of the 2010s much of the phosphorus in the lake comes from fertilizer applied to\n       <a href="/wiki/No-till_farming" title="No-till farming">\n        no-till\n       </a>\n       soybean and corn fields but washed into streams by heavy rains. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Algal_bloom" title="Algal bloom">\n        algal blooms\n       </a>\n       result from growth of\n       <a href="/wiki/Microcystis" title="Microcystis">\n        Microcystis\n       </a>\n       , a toxic\n       <a href="/wiki/Cyanobacteria" title="Cyanobacteria">\n        blue-green algae\n       </a>\n       that the\n       <a href="/wiki/Zebra_mussel" title="Zebra mussel">\n        zebra mussels\n       </a>\n       which infest the lake don\'t eat.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT031413_12-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT031413-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There periodically is a\n       <i>\n        dead zone\n       </i>\n       , or region of low oxygen, in the lake whose exact location varies. Scientists from the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">\n        National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration\n       </a>\n       have been studying the lake\'s blue-green algae blooms, and trying to find ways to predict when they are spreading or where they might hit landfall; typically the blooms arrive late each summer.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX412a_13-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX412a-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This problem was extreme in the mid and late 1960\'s and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Angelo_F._Coniglio" title="Angelo F. Coniglio">\n        Lake Erie Wastewater Management Study\n       </a>\n       (LEWMS) conducted by the Buffalo District of the US Army\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Corps_of_Engineers" title="United States Army Corps of Engineers">\n        Corps of Engineers\n       </a>\n       determined that the eutrophication was due to "point sources" such as industrial outfalls and municipal sanitary and storm sewer outfalls, as well as "diffuse sources", such as overland runoff from farm and forest land. All these sources contribute nutrients, primarily\n       <a href="/wiki/Phosphorus" title="Phosphorus">\n        phosphorus\n       </a>\n       , to the lake. Growth of organisms in the lake is then spiked to the point that oxygen levels are depleted. LEWMS made recommendations for reducing point source outflows, as well as reducing farm contributions of phosphorus by changing fertilizer usage, employing "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/No-till" title="No-till">\n        no-till\n       </a>\n       " farming and other conservative practices. Many industrial and municipal sources have since then been greatly reduced. The improved farming practices, which were voluntary, were followed for a while, resulting in remarkable recovery of the lake in the 1970s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">\n        <a href="#cite_note-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Unfortunately, the conservative practices are not monitored, and have not been kept up. One recent account suggests that the seasonal algae blooms in Lake Erie were possibly caused by "runoff from cities, fertilizers, zebra mussels, and livestock near water."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX412a_13-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX412a-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A second report focuses on the zebra mussels as being the cause of "big oxygen-poor dead zones" since they filter so much sediment that they have resulted in the growth of algae.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX312a_52-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX312a-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One report suggests the oxygen-poor zone began about 1993 in the lake\'s central basin and becomes more pronounced during summer months, but it is somewhat of a mystery why this happens.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX414_80-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX414-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some scientists speculate that the dead zone is a naturally occurring phenomenon.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ28a_76-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ28a-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Another report cited Ohio\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Maumee_River" title="Maumee River">\n        Maumee River\n       </a>\n       as the main source of polluted runoff of\n       <a href="/wiki/Phosphorus" title="Phosphorus">\n        phosphorus\n       </a>\n       from industries, municipalities, tributaries and agriculture, and in 2008, satellite images showed the algal bloom heading toward Pelee Island, and possibly heading to Lake Erie\'s central basin.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ28a_76-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ28a-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There have been two-year $2 million studies trying to understand the "growing zone" which was described as a "10-foot-thick layer of cold water at the bottom", 55 feet (17\xc2\xa0m) in one area, which stretches "100 miles across the lake\'s center".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX414_80-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX414-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It kills fish and microscopic creatures of the lake\'s food chain and fouls the water, and may cause further problems in later years for sport and commercial fishing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX414_80-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX414-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Algae blooms continued in early 2013 but new farming techniques,\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">\n        climate change\n       </a>\n       and even a change in Lake Erie\xe2\x80\x99s ecosystem make phosphorus pollution more intractable.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">\n        <a href="#cite_note-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Snakes">\n        Snakes\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Snakes">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nerodia_sipedonPCSL02111B1.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="385" data-file-width="512" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Nerodia_sipedonPCSL02111B1.jpg/220px-Nerodia_sipedonPCSL02111B1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Nerodia_sipedonPCSL02111B1.jpg/330px-Nerodia_sipedonPCSL02111B1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Nerodia_sipedonPCSL02111B1.jpg/440px-Nerodia_sipedonPCSL02111B1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nerodia_sipedonPCSL02111B1.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The northern watersnake (\n         <i>\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nerodia_sipedon" title="Nerodia sipedon">\n           Nerodia sipedon\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         ) is nonvenomous.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Lake Erie water snake, a subspecies of the northern water snake (\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nerodia_sipedon" title="Nerodia sipedon">\n         Nerodia sipedon\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ), lives in the vicinity of Ohio\'s Put-in-Bay Harbor, and had been put on the threatened species list.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX12_82-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX12-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A\n       <a href="/wiki/Threatened_species" title="Threatened species">\n        threatened species\n       </a>\n       is one which may soon become an\n       <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">\n        endangered species\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX13_83-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX13-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By 2010, the water snake population was over 12,000 snakes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX12_82-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX12-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       While they have a non-venomous bite, they are a key predator in the lake\'s aquatic ecosystem since they feed on\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mudpuppies" title="Mudpuppies">\n        mudpuppies\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Walleye" title="Walleye">\n        walleye\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Smallmouth_bass" title="Smallmouth bass">\n        smallmouth bass\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX12_82-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX12-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The snake was helpful in keeping the population of\n       <a href="/wiki/Goby" title="Goby">\n        goby\n       </a>\n       fish in check.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX12_82-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX12-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They mate from late May through early June and can be found in large\n       <i>\n        mating balls\n       </i>\n       with one female bunched with several males.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX13_83-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX13-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Asian_carp">\n        Asian carp\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Asian carp">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       There is a concern that\n       <a href="/wiki/Asian_carp" title="Asian carp">\n        Asian carp\n       </a>\n       might enter the Great Lakes region and alter the ecosystem negatively.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX14b_42-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX14b-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They have been described as "greedy giants that suck plankton from the water with the brutal efficiency of vacuum cleaners" and scientists worry that they may unravel the "aquatic food web" by crowding out other species.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX14b_42-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX14b-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Snakehead_fish">\n        Snakehead fish\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Snakehead fish">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Northern_snakehead.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="192" data-file-width="700" height="60" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Northern_snakehead.jpg/220px-Northern_snakehead.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Northern_snakehead.jpg/330px-Northern_snakehead.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Northern_snakehead.jpg/440px-Northern_snakehead.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Northern_snakehead.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Snakehead fish\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       There was concern in 2007 that\n       <a href="/wiki/Snakehead_(fish)" title="Snakehead (fish)">\n        snakehead\n       </a>\n       fish could get into the Great Lakes area.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ44_84-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ44-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Officials warn that if the fish invades, it could "decimate the aquatic food chain".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ44_84-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ44-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A YouTube video mentioned in a newspaper account has a man claiming that the fish could "bite your entire hand off". The fish can reach 5\xc2\xa0feet 11\xc2\xa0inches (1.80\xc2\xa0m) in length and "survive out of water for four days" and "has a mouth full of teeth that can shear fish in half" and can "eat ducks and small mammals."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ44_84-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ44-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It should be noted however the snakehead fish can not live in a lake that has completely frozen over. They must come to the surface to breathe via their swim bladder.\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        It gets such huge sizes. It moves over land and it breathes air and it will eat anything it comes into contact with. That\'s what freaks people out about it, to see a fish moving across land gulping air.\n       </p>\n       <div class="templatequotecite">\n        \xe2\x80\x94\n        <cite>\n         about the Snakehead fish, 2007,\n         <i>\n          CanWest News Service\n         </i>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ44_84-3">\n          <a href="#cite_note-twsZ44-84">\n           [84]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </cite>\n       </div>\n      </blockquote>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture_and_life_around_the_lake">\n        Agriculture and life around the lake\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Agriculture and life around the lake">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       In 1999, Doppler radar weather sensors detected millions of mayflies heading for Presque Isle in blue and green splotches on the radar in clouds measuring ten miles (16\xc2\xa0km) long.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX24_85-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX24-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These insects were a sign of Lake Erie\'s move back to health, since the mayflies require clean water to thrive.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX24_85-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX24-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Biologist Masteller of\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_State_University" title="Pennsylvania State University">\n        Penn State Erie\n       </a>\n       declared the bugs to be a "nice nuisance" since they signified the lake\'s return to health after forty years of absence.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX24_85-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX24-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Each is an inch and a half long; the three main species of mayflies are\n       <i>\n        Ephemera simulans\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        Hexagenia rigida\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        Hexagenia limbata\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX24_85-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX24-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The insects mate over a 72-hour period from June through September; they fly in masses up to the shore, mate in the air, then females lay up to 8,000 eggs each over the water; the eggs sink back down and the cycle repeats.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX24_85-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX24-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Sometimes the clouds of mayflies have caused power outages\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX37_86-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX37-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       as well as causing roads to become slippery with squashed insects.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX24_85-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX24-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Since\n       <a href="/wiki/Zebra_mussel" title="Zebra mussel">\n        zebra mussels\n       </a>\n       filter extra nutrients from the lake, it allows the mayfly larvae to thrive.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX37_86-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX37-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cygnus_buccinator_-Lake_Erie,_Michigan,_USA-8_(1).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1386" data-file-width="1940" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Cygnus_buccinator_-Lake_Erie%2C_Michigan%2C_USA-8_%281%29.jpg/220px-Cygnus_buccinator_-Lake_Erie%2C_Michigan%2C_USA-8_%281%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Cygnus_buccinator_-Lake_Erie%2C_Michigan%2C_USA-8_%281%29.jpg/330px-Cygnus_buccinator_-Lake_Erie%2C_Michigan%2C_USA-8_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Cygnus_buccinator_-Lake_Erie%2C_Michigan%2C_USA-8_%281%29.jpg/440px-Cygnus_buccinator_-Lake_Erie%2C_Michigan%2C_USA-8_%281%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cygnus_buccinator_-Lake_Erie,_Michigan,_USA-8_(1).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/Trumpeter_swan" title="Trumpeter swan">\n          trumpeter swan\n         </a>\n         (\n         <i>\n          Cygnus buccinator\n         </i>\n         ) on Lake Erie\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       There have been incidents of birds dying from\n       <a href="/wiki/Botulism" title="Botulism">\n        botulism\n       </a>\n       , in 2000,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX31_87-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX31-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and in 2002.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX26_88-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX26-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Birds affected included grebes, common and red-breasted mergansers, loons, diving ducks, ring-billed gulls and herring gulls.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX31_87-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX31-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One account suggests that bird populations are in trouble, notably the woodland warbler, which had population declines around 60 percent in 2008.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX312a_52-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX312a-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Possible causes for declines in bird populations are farming practices, loss of habitats, soil depletion and erosion, and toxic chemicals.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX312a_52-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX312a-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2006, there were concerns of possible\n       <a href="/wiki/Avian_influenza" title="Avian influenza">\n        bird flu\n       </a>\n       after two wild swans on the lake were found diseased, but it was learned that they did not contain the deadly H5N1 virus.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY311_89-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY311-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There were sightings of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Magnificent_frigatebird" title="Magnificent frigatebird">\n        magnificent frigatebird\n       </a>\n       , a tropical bird with a two-metre wingspan, over the lake in 2008.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ34_90-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ34-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Water_quality_issues_and_restoration">\n        Water quality issues and restoration\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Water quality issues and restoration">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Lake Erie infamously became very polluted in the 1960s and 1970s as a result of the quantity of\n       <a href="/wiki/Heavy_industry" title="Heavy industry">\n        heavy industry\n       </a>\n       situated in cities on its shores, with reports of bacteria-laden beaches and fish contaminated by industrial waste.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ36_91-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ36-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the 1970s, patches of the lake were declared dead because of\n       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_waste" title="Industrial waste">\n        industrial waste\n       </a>\n       as well as sewage from runoffs; as\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">\n         The New York Times\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       reporter Denny Lee wrote in 2004, "The lake, after all, is where the\n       <a href="/wiki/Rust_Belt" title="Rust Belt">\n        Rust Belt\n       </a>\n       meets the water."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX43d_17-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX43d-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Water_quality" title="Water quality">\n        water quality\n       </a>\n       deteriorated partially due to increasing levels of the nutrient\n       <a href="/wiki/Phosphorus" title="Phosphorus">\n        phosphorus\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ28a_76-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ28a-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       in both the water and lake bottom sediments. The resultant high\n       <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">\n        nitrogen\n       </a>\n       levels in the water caused\n       <a href="/wiki/Eutrophication" title="Eutrophication">\n        eutrophication\n       </a>\n       , which resulted in\n       <a href="/wiki/Algal_bloom" title="Algal bloom">\n        algal blooms\n       </a>\n       and algae masses\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX215_92-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX215-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fish_kill" title="Fish kill">\n        fish kills\n       </a>\n       increasingly fouled the shoreline during this period. There were incidents of the oily surfaces of tributary rivers emptying into Lake Erie catching fire: in 1969, Cleveland\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Cuyahoga_River" title="Cuyahoga River">\n        Cuyahoga River\n       </a>\n       erupted in flames,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX215_92-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX215-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       chronicled in a\n       <i>\n        Time\n       </i>\n       magazine article which lamented a tendency to use rivers flowing through major cities as "convenient, free sewers";\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY214a_53-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY214a-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_River" title="Detroit River">\n        Detroit River\n       </a>\n       caught fire on another occasion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX312a_52-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX312a-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The outlook was gloomy:\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        Each day, Detroit, Cleveland and 120 other municipalities fill Erie with 1.5 billion gallons of "inadequately treated wastes, including nitrates and phosphates ... These chemicals act as fertilizer for growths of algae that suck oxygen from the lower depths and rise to the surface as odoriferous green scum ... Commercial and game fish\xe2\x80\x94blue pike, whitefish, sturgeon, northern pike\xe2\x80\x94have nearly vanished, yielding the waters to trash fish that need less\n        <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">\n         oxygen\n        </a>\n        . Weeds proliferate, turning water frontage into swamp. In short, Lake Erie is in danger of dying by suffocation.\n       </p>\n       <div class="templatequotecite">\n        \xe2\x80\x94\n        <cite>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">\n           Time\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         magazine, August 1969\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY214a_53-4">\n          <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY214a-53">\n           [53]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </cite>\n       </div>\n      </blockquote>\n      <p>\n       These events embarrassed officials and spurred local officials, including Cleveland\'s director of public utilities, Ben Stefanski, to pursue a massive effort to "scrub the Cuyahoga"; the effort cost $100 million in bonds, according to one estimate.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY214a_53-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY214a-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       New sewer lines were built.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY214a_53-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY214a-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Clevelanders approved a bond issue by 2 to 1 to seriously upgrade Cleveland\'s sewage system.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY214a_53-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY214a-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Federal officials acted as well; the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">\n        United States Congress\n       </a>\n       passed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Clean_Water_Act" title="Clean Water Act">\n        Clean Water Act\n       </a>\n       of 1972.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX215_92-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX215-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In that year, the United States and Canada established\n       <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution" title="Water pollution">\n        water pollution\n       </a>\n       limits in an International Water Quality Agreement. The\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Corps_of_Engineers" title="United States Army Corps of Engineers">\n        Corps\n       </a>\n       \' LEWMS, mentioned above, was also instituted at that time. The controls were effective, but it took several decades to take effect; by 1999, there were signs that large numbers of mayflies were spotted on the lake after a forty-year absence, signalling a return to health.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX43d_17-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX43d-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX24_85-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX24-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The clearing of the water column is also partly due to the introduction and rapid spread of\n       <a href="/wiki/Zebra_mussel" title="Zebra mussel">\n        zebra mussels\n       </a>\n       from\n       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">\n        Europe\n       </a>\n       , which had the effect of covering "the basin floor like shag carpeting" with each creature filtering "a liter of fresh water a day," helping to restore the lake to a cleaner state.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX43d_17-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX43d-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The 1972 Great Lakes Water Quality Agreement also significantly reduced the dumping and runoff of phosphorus into the lake. The lake has since become clean enough to allow sunlight to infiltrate its water and produce algae and sea weed, but a dead zone persists in the central\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie_Basin" title="Lake Erie Basin">\n        Lake Erie Basin\n       </a>\n       during the late summer. The\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">\n        United States Environmental Protection Agency\n       </a>\n       has studied this cyclic phenomenon since 2005.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n        <a href="#cite_note-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There have been instances of beach closings at\n       <a href="/wiki/Presque_Isle_State_Park" title="Presque Isle State Park">\n        Presque Isle\n       </a>\n       off the coast of northwestern Pennsylvania because of unexplained E. Coli contaminations,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX22a_95-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX22a-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       possibly caused by storm water overflows after heavy downpours.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CLEVELAND_SKYLINE_AND_LAKE_ERIE_AT_DAYBREAK_-_NARA_-_550291.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2036" data-file-width="3000" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/CLEVELAND_SKYLINE_AND_LAKE_ERIE_AT_DAYBREAK_-_NARA_-_550291.jpg/220px-CLEVELAND_SKYLINE_AND_LAKE_ERIE_AT_DAYBREAK_-_NARA_-_550291.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/CLEVELAND_SKYLINE_AND_LAKE_ERIE_AT_DAYBREAK_-_NARA_-_550291.jpg/330px-CLEVELAND_SKYLINE_AND_LAKE_ERIE_AT_DAYBREAK_-_NARA_-_550291.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/CLEVELAND_SKYLINE_AND_LAKE_ERIE_AT_DAYBREAK_-_NARA_-_550291.jpg/440px-CLEVELAND_SKYLINE_AND_LAKE_ERIE_AT_DAYBREAK_-_NARA_-_550291.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CLEVELAND_SKYLINE_AND_LAKE_ERIE_AT_DAYBREAK_-_NARA_-_550291.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Daybreak with\n         <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">\n          Cleveland\n         </a>\n         skyline\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cleveland_sunset.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Cleveland_sunset.jpg/220px-Cleveland_sunset.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Cleveland_sunset.jpg/330px-Cleveland_sunset.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Cleveland_sunset.jpg/440px-Cleveland_sunset.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cleveland_sunset.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Sunset from Cleveland pier\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Since the 1970s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_regulation" title="Environmental regulation">\n        environmental regulation\n       </a>\n       has led to a great increase in water quality and the return of economically important fish species such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Walleye" title="Walleye">\n        walleye\n       </a>\n       and other biological life.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">\n        <a href="#cite_note-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There was substantial evidence that the new controls had substantially reduced levels of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DDT" title="DDT">\n        DDT\n       </a>\n       in the water by 1979.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX215cc_27-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX215cc-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Cleanup efforts were described in 1979 as a notable environmental success story, suggesting that the cumulative effect of legislation, studies, and bans had reversed the effects of pollution:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX215cc_27-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX215cc-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        The globs of oil, the multicolored industrial discharges, the flotsam from shoreline cities, the fecal and bacterial wastes are no longer dumped in the lakes in vast quantities.\n       </p>\n       <div class="templatequotecite">\n        \xe2\x80\x94\n        <cite>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">\n           Time\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         magazine, 1979\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX215cc_27-3">\n          <a href="#cite_note-twsX215cc-27">\n           [27]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </cite>\n       </div>\n      </blockquote>\n      <p>\n       Joint U.S.\xe2\x80\x93Canadian agreements pushed 600 of 864 major industrial dischargers to meet requirements for keeping the water clean.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX215cc_27-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX215cc-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One estimate was that $5\xc2\xa0billion was spent to upgrade plants to treat sewage.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX215cc_27-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX215cc-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The change toward cleaner water has been in a positive direction since the 1970s.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_ecosystem_related_issues">\n        Other ecosystem related issues\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Other ecosystem related issues">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       There was a tentative exploratory plan to capture\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">\n        CO\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n       </a>\n       , compress it to a liquid form, and pump it a half-mile (800 m) beneath Lake Erie\'s surface underneath the porous rock structure.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ62_97-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ62-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       According to\n       <a href="/wiki/Chemical_engineering" title="Chemical engineering">\n        chemical engineer\n       </a>\n       Peter Douglas, there is sufficient storage space beneath Lake Erie to hold between 15 and 50 years of liquid CO2 emissions from the 4,000 megawatt Nanticoke coal plant.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ62_97-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ62-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       But there has been no substantial progress on this issue since 2007.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">\n        Economy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Economy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fishing">\n        Fishing\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Fishing">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Species_of_fish">\n        Species of fish\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Species of fish">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Erie_07-04-2008_01;14;23PM.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="615" data-file-width="879" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Erie_07-04-2008_01%3B14%3B23PM.JPG/220px-Erie_07-04-2008_01%3B14%3B23PM.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Erie_07-04-2008_01%3B14%3B23PM.JPG/330px-Erie_07-04-2008_01%3B14%3B23PM.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Erie_07-04-2008_01%3B14%3B23PM.JPG/440px-Erie_07-04-2008_01%3B14%3B23PM.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Erie_07-04-2008_01;14;23PM.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Summer morning west of\n         <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">\n          Cleveland\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Lake Erie is home to one of the world\'s largest freshwater commercial fisheries. Lake Erie\'s fish populations are the most abundant of the Great Lakes, partially because of the lake\'s relatively mild temperatures and plentiful supply of\n       <a href="/wiki/Plankton" title="Plankton">\n        plankton\n       </a>\n       , which is the basic building block of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Food_chain" title="Food chain">\n        food chain\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX14b_42-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX14b-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The lake\'s fish population accounts for an estimated 50% of all fish inhabiting the Great Lakes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">\n        <a href="#cite_note-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The lake is "loaded with superstars" such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_trout" title="Rainbow trout">\n        steelhead\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ14_99-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ14-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Walleye" title="Walleye">\n        walleye\n       </a>\n       (American usage) or\n       <a href="/wiki/Esox" title="Esox">\n        pickerel\n       </a>\n       (Canadian usage),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX14b_42-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX14b-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ14_99-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ14-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Smallmouth_bass" title="Smallmouth bass">\n        smallmouth bass\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ14_99-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ14-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Perch" title="Perch">\n        perch\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ14_99-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ14-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       as well as bass, trout, salmon, whitefesh, smelt, and many others.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX14b_42-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX14b-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The lake consists of a long list of well established\n       <a href="/wiki/Introduced_species" title="Introduced species">\n        introduced species\n       </a>\n       . Common non-indigenous fish species include the\n       <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_smelt" title="Rainbow smelt">\n        rainbow smelt\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Alewife" title="Alewife">\n        alewife\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/White_perch" title="White perch">\n        white perch\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Common_carp" title="Common carp">\n        common carp\n       </a>\n       . Non-native sport fish such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_trout" title="Rainbow trout">\n        rainbow trout\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Brown_trout" title="Brown trout">\n        brown trout\n       </a>\n       are stocked specifically for anglers to catch. Attempts failed to stock\n       <a href="/wiki/Coho_salmon" title="Coho salmon">\n        coho salmon\n       </a>\n       and its numbers are once again dwindling. Commercial landings are dominated by yellow perch and\n       <a href="/wiki/Walleye" title="Walleye">\n        walleye\n       </a>\n       , with substantial quantities of\n       <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_smelt" title="Rainbow smelt">\n        rainbow smelt\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/White_bass" title="White bass">\n        white bass\n       </a>\n       also taken. Anglers target walleye and yellow perch, with some effort directed at\n       <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_trout" title="Rainbow trout">\n        rainbow trout\n       </a>\n       . A variety of other species are taken in smaller quantities by both commercial and sport fleets.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Up until the end of the 1950s, the most commonly caught commercial fish (more than 50% of the commercial catch) was a subspecies of the walleye known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Blue_walleye" title="Blue walleye">\n        blue walleye\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        Sander vitreus glaucus\n       </i>\n       ) sometimes erroneously called "blue pike". In the 1970s and 1980s, as pollution in the lake declined, counts of walleyes which were caught grew from 112,000 in 1975 to 4.1 million in 1985, with estimates of the numbers of walleyes in the lake at around 33 million in the basin, with many of 8 pounds or more.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsJanY211_100-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsJanY211-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Not all walleyes thrived. The combination of overfishing and the eutrophication of the lake by pollution caused the population to collapse, and in the mid-1980s, one species of walleye called the\n       <a href="/wiki/Blue_walleye" title="Blue walleye">\n        blue walleye\n       </a>\n       was declared extinct. But the Lake Erie walleye was reportedly having record numbers, even in 1989, according to one report.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX41_101-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX41-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There have been concerns about rising levels of mercury in walleye fish; a study by the Canadian Ministry of the Environment noted an "increasing concentration trend" but that limits were within acceptable established by authorities in\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">\n        Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX511_102-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX511-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It was recommended, because of PCBs, that persons eat no more than one walleye meal per month.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX511_102-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX511-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Because of these and other concerns, in 1990, the National Wildlife Federation was on the verge of having a "negative fish consumption\n       <i>\n        advisory\n       </i>\n       " for walleyes and smallmouth bass, which had been the bread-and-butter catch of an $800 million commercial fishing industry.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX513_103-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX513-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The longest fish in Lake Erie is reportedly the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sturgeon" title="Sturgeon">\n        sturgeon\n       </a>\n       which can grow to ten feet long and weight 300 pounds, but it is an\n       <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">\n        endangered species\n       </a>\n       and mostly lives on the bottom of the lake.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX27a_104-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX27a-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2009, there was a confirmed instance of a sturgeon being caught, which was returned to the lake alive, and there are hopes that the population of sturgeons is resurging.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX32_105-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX32-105">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_fishing">\n        Commercial fishing\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Commercial fishing">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lake_Erie_Sunset_with_fish_net.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Lake_Erie_Sunset_with_fish_net.JPG/220px-Lake_Erie_Sunset_with_fish_net.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Lake_Erie_Sunset_with_fish_net.JPG/330px-Lake_Erie_Sunset_with_fish_net.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Lake_Erie_Sunset_with_fish_net.JPG/440px-Lake_Erie_Sunset_with_fish_net.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lake_Erie_Sunset_with_fish_net.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Sunset on Lake Erie seen through a fishing net\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Estimates vary about the fishing market for the Great Lakes region. One estimate of the total market for fishing, including commercial as well as sport or recreational fishing, for all of the Great Lakes, was $4 billion annually, in 2007.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX412a_13-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX412a-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A second estimate was that the fishing industry was valued at more than $7 billion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX14b_42-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX14b-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       But since high levels of\n       <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">\n        pollution\n       </a>\n       were discovered in the 1960s and 1970s, there has been continued debate over the desired intensity of commercial fishing.\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_fishing" title="Commercial fishing">\n        Commercial fishing\n       </a>\n       in Lake Erie has been hurt by the bad economy as well as government regulations which limit the size of their catch; one report suggested that the numbers of fishing boats and employees had declined by two-thirds in recent decades.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX14b_42-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX14b-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Another concern had been that pollution in the lake, as well as toxins found inside fish, were working against commercial fishing interests.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX215_92-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX215-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       U.S. fishermen based along Lake Erie "lost their livelihood" over the past few decades described as being "caught in a net of laws and bans", according to the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Post-Gazette" title="Pittsburgh Post-Gazette">\n         Pittsburgh Post-Gazette\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , and no longer catch fish such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Whitefish_(fisheries_term)" title="Whitefish (fisheries term)">\n        whitefish\n       </a>\n       for markets in New York.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX314a_23-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX314a-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Pennsylvania had a special $3 stamp on fishing licenses to help "compensate commercial fishermen for their losses", but this program ended after five years turning Erie\'s commercial fishing industry into an "artifact."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX314a_23-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX314a-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One blamed the commercial fishing ban after a "test of wills" between commercial and recreational fishermen: "One side needed large hauls. The other feared the lake was being emptied."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX314a_23-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX314a-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Commercial fishing is now predominantly based in Canadian communities, with a much smaller fishery\xe2\x80\x94largely restricted to\n       <a href="/wiki/Yellow_perch" title="Yellow perch">\n        yellow perch\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94in Ohio. One account suggested that Canadian fishermen are "still at it and making money" and they "know how to fish" by "using the old nets."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX314a_23-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX314a-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Ontario fishery is one of the most intensively managed in the world. However, there are reports that some Canadian commercial fishermen are dissatisfied with fishing quotas, and have sued their government about this matter, and there have been complaints that the legislative body writing the quotas is "dominated by the U.S." and that sport fishing interests are favored at the expense of commercial fishing interests.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ32_106-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ32-106">\n         [106]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Cuts of 30 to 45 percent for certain fish were made in 2007.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsZ32_106-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsZ32-106">\n         [106]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Lake Erie fishery was one of the first fisheries in the world managed on individual transferable quotas and features mandatory daily catch reporting and intensive auditing of the catch reporting system. Still, the commercial fishery is the target of critics who would like to see the lake managed for the exclusive benefit of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sport_fishing" title="Sport fishing">\n        sport fishing\n       </a>\n       and the various industries serving the sport fishery. In November 2010, Ontario\'s oldest and largest fish processor known as Great Lakes Fish Corporation was shut down after operating for a hundred years; 130 workers were laid off and numerous spinoff jobs disappeared, such as jobs at local restaurants and net repair shops.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX14f_107-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX14f-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       According to one report, the Canadian town of\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_Dover,_Ontario" title="Port Dover, Ontario">\n        Port Dover\n       </a>\n       is the home of the lake\'s largest fishing fleet, and the town features miniature golf, dairy bars, French-fry stands, and restaurants serving\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perch_(fish)" title="Perch (fish)">\n        perch\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsX18_22-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-twsX18-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government_regulation_of_fishing">\n        Government regulation of fishing\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Erie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Government regulation of fishing">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The lake can be thought of as a common asset with multiple purposes including being a\n       <i>\n        fishery\n       </i>\n       . There was direct competition between commercial fishermen and sport fishermen (including charter boats and sales of fishing licenses) throughout the lake\'s history, with both sides seeking government
